<initialization>

    Create (or update) a concise AGENTS.md file that enables immediate productivity for AI assistants.
    Focus ONLY on project-specific, non-obvious information that you had to discover by reading files.
    
    CRITICAL: Only include information that is:
    - Non-obvious (couldn't be guessed from standard practices)
    - Project-specific (not generic to the framework/language)
    - Discovered by reading files (config files, code patterns, custom utilities)
    - Essential for avoiding mistakes or following project conventions
    
    Usage notes:
    - The file you create will be given to agentic coding agents (such as yourself) that operate in this repository
    - Keep the main AGENTS.md concise - aim for about 20 lines, but use more if the project complexity requires it
    - If there's already an AGENTS.md, improve it
    - If there are Claude Code rules (in CLAUDE.md), Cursor rules (in .cursor/rules/ or .cursorrules), or Copilot rules (in .github/copilot-instructions.md), make sure to include them
    - Be sure to prefix the file with: "# AGENTS.md\n\nThis file provides guidance to agents when working with code in this repository."
  </purpose>
  
  <todo_list_creation>
    If the update_todo_list tool is available, create a todo list with these focused analysis steps:
    
    1. Check for existing AGENTS.md files
       CRITICAL - Check these EXACT paths IN THE PROJECT ROOT:

<analysis_workflow>
  Follow the comprehensive analysis workflow to:

     CRITICAL - First check for existing AGENTS.md files at these EXACT locations IN PROJECT ROOT:

     - What information is OBVIOUS and must be DELETED?

     - The file should get SHORTER, not longer
     
     Also find other AI assistant rules and documentation
     
  2. **Project Identification**: Identify language, stack, and build system
  3. **Command Extraction**: Extract and verify essential commands
  4. **Architecture Mapping**: Create visual flow diagrams of core processes

</analysis_workflow>

<output_structure>
  <main_file>
    Create or deeply improve AGENTS.md with ONLY non-obvious information:
    
    If AGENTS.md exists:
    - FIRST: Delete ALL obvious information
    - REMOVE: Standard commands, framework defaults, common patterns
    - STRIP: Anything that doesn't require file reading to know
    - EVALUATE: Each line - would an experienced dev be surprised?
    - If not surprised, DELETE IT
    - THEN: Add only truly non-obvious new discoveries
    - Goal: File should be SHORTER and MORE VALUABLE
    
    Content should include:
    - Header: "# AGENTS.md\n\nThis file provides guidance to agents when working with code in this repository."
    - Build/lint/test commands - ONLY if they differ from standard package.json scripts
    - Code style - ONLY project-specific rules not covered by linter configs
    - Custom utilities or patterns discovered by reading the code
    - Non-standard directory structures or file organizations
    - Project-specific conventions that violate typical practices
    - Critical gotchas that would cause errors if not followed
    
    EXCLUDE obvious information like:
    - Standard npm/yarn commands visible in package.json
    - Framework defaults (e.g., "React uses JSX")
    - Common patterns (e.g., "tests go in __tests__ folders")
    - Information derivable from file extensions or directory names
    
    Keep it concise (aim for ~20 lines, but expand as needed for complex projects).
    Include existing AI assistant rules from CLAUDE.md, Cursor rules (.cursor/rules/ or .cursorrules), or Copilot rules (.github/copilot-instructions.md).
  </main_file>
  
  <mode_specific_files>
    Create or deeply improve mode-specific AGENTS.md files IN THE PROJECT ROOT.
    
    CRITICAL: For each of these paths (RELATIVE TO PROJECT ROOT), check if the file exists FIRST:
    - .roo/rules-code/AGENTS.md (create .roo in project root, not system root!)
    - .roo/rules-debug/AGENTS.md (relative to project root)
    - .roo/rules-ask/AGENTS.md (relative to project root)
    - .roo/rules-architect/AGENTS.md (relative to project root)
    
    IMPORTANT: The .roo directory must be created in the current project/workspace root directory,
    NOT at the system root (/) or home directory. All paths are relative to where the project is located.
    
    If files exist:
    - AGGRESSIVELY DELETE obvious information
    - Remove EVERYTHING that's standard practice
    - Strip out framework defaults and common patterns
    - Each remaining line must be surprising/non-obvious
    - Only then add new non-obvious discoveries
    - Files should become SHORTER, not longer
    
    Example structure (ALL IN PROJECT ROOT):
    ```
    project-root/
    ├── AGENTS.md                    # General project guidance
    ├── .roo/                        # IN PROJECT ROOT, NOT SYSTEM ROOT!
    │   ├── rules-code/
    │   │   └── AGENTS.md           # Code mode specific instructions
    │   ├── rules-debug/
    │   │   └── AGENTS.md           # Debug mode specific instructions
    │   ├── rules-ask/
    │   │   └── AGENTS.md           # Ask mode specific instructions
    │   └── rules-architect/
    │       └── AGENTS.md           # Architect mode specific instructions
    ├── src/
    ├── package.json
    └── ... other project files
    ```
    
    .roo/rules-code/AGENTS.md - ONLY non-obvious coding rules discovered by reading files:
    - Custom utilities that replace standard approaches
    - Non-standard patterns unique to this project
    - Hidden dependencies or coupling between components
    - Required import orders or naming conventions not enforced by linters
    
    Example of non-obvious rules worth documenting:
    ```
    # Project Coding Rules (Non-Obvious Only)
    - Always use safeWriteJson() from src/utils/ instead of JSON.stringify for file writes (prevents corruption)
    - API retry mechanism in src/api/providers/utils/ is mandatory (not optional as it appears)
    - Database queries MUST use the query builder pattern (raw SQL will fail)
    - Provider interface in packages/types/src/ has undocumented required methods
    - Test files must be in same directory as source for vitest to work (not in separate test folder)
    ```
    
    .roo/rules-debug/AGENTS.md - ONLY non-obvious debugging discoveries:
    - Hidden log locations not mentioned in docs
    - Non-standard debugging tools or flags
    - Gotchas that cause silent failures
    - Required environment variables for debugging
    
    Example of non-obvious debug rules worth documenting:
    ```
    # Project Debug Rules (Non-Obvious Only)
    - Webview dev tools accessed via Command Palette > "Developer: Open Webview Developer Tools" (not F12)
    - IPC messages fail silently if not wrapped in try/catch in packages/ipc/src/
    - Production builds require NODE_ENV=production or certain features break without error
    - Database migrations must run from the correct package directory, not root
    - Extension logs only visible in "Extension Host" output channel, not Debug Console
    ```
    
    .roo/rules-ask/AGENTS.md - ONLY non-obvious documentation context:
    - Hidden or misnamed documentation
    - Counterintuitive code organization
    - Misleading folder names or structures
    - Important context not evident from file structure
    
    Example of non-obvious documentation rules worth documenting:
    ```
    # Project Documentation Rules (Non-Obvious Only)
    - "src/" contains VSCode extension code, not source for web apps (counterintuitive)
    - Provider examples in src/api/providers/ are the canonical reference (docs are outdated)
    - UI runs in VSCode webview with restrictions (no localStorage, limited APIs)
    - Package.json scripts must be run from specific directories, not root
    - Locales in root are for extension, webview-ui/src/i18n for UI (two separate systems)
    ```
    
    .roo/rules-architect/AGENTS.md - ONLY non-obvious architectural constraints:
    - Hidden coupling between components
    - Undocumented architectural decisions
    - Non-standard patterns that must be followed
    - Performance bottlenecks discovered through investigation
    
    Example of non-obvious architecture rules worth documenting:
    ```
    # Project Architecture Rules (Non-Obvious Only)
    - Providers MUST be stateless - hidden caching layer assumes this
    - Webview and extension communicate through specific IPC channel patterns only
    - Database migrations cannot be rolled back - forward-only by design
    - React hooks required because external state libraries break webview isolation
    - Monorepo packages have circular dependency on types package (intentional)
    ```
  </mode_specific_files>
</output_structure>

Now I'll delegate the comprehensive audit of both projects to specialized modes. Let me create two parallel analysis tasks. 
[Tool Use: new_task]
Mode: architect
Message: You are tasked with performing a comprehensive architectural audit of the Computer-Use project (located at d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Computer-Use). This is the first phase of converting an experimental prototype into a production-grade application.

## Scope
Analyze the entire Computer-Use project and provide a detailed audit report covering:

1. **Project Purpose & Architecture**
   - What is this project's primary purpose?
   - What is the overall system architecture?
   - How do components interact?
   - What are the main entry points?

2. **Current State Assessment**
   - List all major components and their responsibilities
   - Document the technology stack (languages, frameworks, libraries)
   - Identify all dependencies and their versions
   - Map the project structure (src/, bridges/, platforms/, etc.)

3. **Critical Issues & Technical Debt**
   - Identify any obvious architectural flaws
   - Document missing error handling patterns
   - List potential security vulnerabilities
   - Note scalability limitations
   - Identify performance bottlenecks
   - Document any hardcoded values or configuration issues

4. **Code Quality Assessment**
   - Are there inconsistent patterns across modules?
   - Are there duplicate code blocks that should be refactored?
   - Is error handling comprehensive?
   - Are there missing edge case handlers?
   - Document type safety issues (if applicable)

5. **Production Readiness Gaps**
   - What's missing for production deployment?
   - Logging and monitoring capabilities
   - Configuration management
   - Graceful shutdown procedures
   - Health check endpoints/mechanisms
   - Rate limiting and throttling
   - Resource cleanup

6. **Feature & Enhancement Opportunities**
   - What new features could add value?
   - What improvements would enhance reliability?
   - What would make it more maintainable?

## Deliverable
Create a comprehensive audit report in markdown format. Include:
- Executive summary of findings
- Detailed sections for each area above
- Prioritized list of issues (Critical, High, Medium, Low)
- Recommended fixes and improvements
- Estimated complexity for each fix

Save this as `AUDIT_COMPUTER_USE.md` in the project root.

When complete, use attempt_completion to signal that the audit is finished and provide a summary of key findings.
Todos: [ ] Explore project structure and understand purpose
[ ] Document architecture and components
[ ] Assess technology stack and dependencies
[ ] Identify critical issues and technical debt
[ ] Evaluate code quality and patterns
[ ] Assess production readiness
[ ] Document feature opportunities
[ ] Create prioritized issues list
[ ] Generate audit report (AUDIT_COMPUTER_USE.md)

## Your Mission

1. **Thoroughly read ALL source files** in the project:
   - All files in `src/` directory (server.py, hybrid_server.py, capture_service.py, speech_processor.py, voice_server.py, overlay.py, ui_elements.py, run_agent.py, config.py, mcp_complex_prompt_llm.py, run_complex_mcp_prompt.py)

   - Check `scratch/` for any test scripts

   - **Project Purpose & Architecture**: What does this project do? How do components interact?
   - **Technology Stack**: Languages, frameworks, all dependencies and versions
   - **Critical Issues**: List every bug, architectural flaw, missing error handling, security vulnerability, scalability limitation
   - **Code Quality**: Inconsistent patterns, duplications, missing type hints, poor naming, hardcoded values, missing edge case handling
   - **Production Readiness Gaps**: Missing logging, monitoring, config management, graceful shutdown, health checks, rate limiting, resource cleanup
   - **Feature Opportunities**: What could make this more useful, reliable, maintainable?
   - **Priority Ranking**: Critical > High > Medium > Low for each issue

3. **Specific areas to audit rigorously**:
   - Error handling: Are all exceptions caught and handled properly?
   - Resource management: Are connections, files, processes properly cleaned up?
   - Configuration: Are secrets hardcoded? Is .env properly used?
   - API design: Are endpoints consistent and well-documented?
   - Concurrency: Are there race conditions or deadlock risks?
   - Dependency management: Are there conflicting or outdated packages?
   - Cross-platform compatibility: Do Windows/Linux scripts work properly?
   - Docker setup: Is the containerization production-ready?

4. **Save your audit report** as `AUDIT_COMPUTER_USE.md` in the project root (overwrite the existing one with a more comprehensive version).

**User:**

[Tool]
Subtask 019ed3fb-97ff-7569-a203-64d67e7cd93c completed.

Result:
The comprehensive architectural audit has been written to [`AUDIT_COMPUTER_USE.md`](AUDIT_COMPUTER_USE.md). Here are the **Top 10 Most Critical Findings**:

---

### 🔴 C1: API Key Leaked in `.env` File
[`.env`](.env:2) contains a real `GEMINI_API_KEY=AIzaSy...` — likely committed to git history. **Immediate action required:** revoke the key, add `.env` to [`.gitignore`](.gitignore), and scrub git history.

### 🔴 C2: Unrestricted Shell Execution — No Sandboxing
The [`bash`](src/server.py:1022-1053) tool passes commands directly to `subprocess` with no allowlisting, no sandboxing, no resource limits. Any MCP client has full user-level system control. The toy filter in [`mcp_complex_prompt_llm.py`](src/mcp_complex_prompt_llm.py:142-162) is trivially bypassable and not applied in the server itself.

### 🔴 C3: Unrestricted Mouse/Keyboard Control — No Confirmation
The [`computer`](src/server.py:460-700) tool can click any coordinate, type any keystrokes, and capture screenshots of sensitive content with zero user confirmation, rate limiting, or audit logging.

### 🔴 C4: Double Registration of `browser_action` and `browser_use_dom`
[`server.py:1237-1238`](src/server.py:1237-1238) explicitly calls `app.add_tool()` for tools that are already registered via `@app.tool()` decorators, causing duplicate tool enumeration — an MCP protocol violation.

### 🔴 C5: Synchronous `mss.grab()` Blocks Async Event Loop
[`_capture_desktop_png_base64()`](src/server.py:607-647) calls `mss.grab()` synchronously inside async functions, blocking the event loop for 20-50ms per call. This causes tool call timeouts, transport stalls, and voice server jitter.

### 🔴 C6: Synchronous `requests` Library in Async Paths
[`call_gemini()`](src/run_agent.py:456) and [`Qwen3TTSProcessor.synthesize_stream()`](src/speech_processor.py:505) use blocking `requests.post()` inside async functions. The project already depends on `httpx` transitively — replace with `httpx.AsyncClient`.

### 🟠 H1: 80+ Bare `except Exception:` Blocks Across Codebase
Nearly every source file swallows exceptions silently. [`overlay.py`](src/overlay.py) alone has ~25 bare catches. This makes debugging impossible and hides real failures from both operators and the VLM.

### 🟠 H2: Temp File Race Condition in ASR Bridge
[`bridges/asr_server.py`](bridges/asr_server.py:55-66) uses PID-based temp file naming (`temp_asr_bridge_{os.getpid()}.wav`) that is neither unique per request nor guaranteed to be cleaned up. Concurrent requests from the same worker will overwrite each other's files.

### 🟠 H3: No Health Checks or Retry Logic for Bridge Endpoints
[`speech_processor.py`](src/speech_processor.py:363-455) accepts `remote_url` for Qwen3 ASR/TTS bridges but never validates connectivity at startup, has no health check, no exponential backoff retry, and surfaces errors only after a full VLM turn is wasted.

### 🟠 H4: `.gitignore` is Incomplete — Sensitive and Generated Files Exposed
[`.gitignore`](.gitignore) only lists 4 patterns (`.history`, `models`, `*.code-workspace`, `screenshots`). Missing: `.env` (API keys!), `__pycache__/`, `*.log`, `logs/`, `scratch/`, virtual environment directories, and `.pyc` files.

---

The full audit document covers **35 source files**, identifies **6 critical**, **9 high**, **11 medium**, and **8 low** issues, includes a Mermaid architecture diagram, complete configuration reference, 4-phase remediation plan, and a pre-production checklist. Maturity rating: **55/100** — meaningful recent improvements (contextvars, pydantic-settings, ShutdownManager, with_timeout) but significant security and reliability gaps remain before production use.

Message: You are tasked with performing a comprehensive architectural audit of the Realtime Dubbing project located at d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing.

This is an experimental prototype that needs to be converted into a production-grade, professionally shippable application. The project is a video dubbing service.

## Your Mission

1. **First, explore the project structure** - list all files recursively to understand the full layout, then read ALL source files thoroughly.

2. **Document the following in detail**:
   - **Project Purpose & Architecture**: What does this project do? How do components interact? What's the data flow for dubbing?
   - **Technology Stack**: Languages, frameworks, all dependencies and versions
   - **Critical Issues**: List every bug, architectural flaw, missing error handling, security vulnerability, scalability limitation
   - **Code Quality**: Inconsistent patterns, duplications, missing type hints, poor naming, hardcoded values, missing edge case handling
   - **Production Readiness Gaps**: Missing logging, monitoring, config management, graceful shutdown, health checks, rate limiting, resource cleanup
   - **Feature Opportunities**: What could make this more useful, reliable, maintainable?
   - **Priority Ranking**: Critical > High > Medium > Low for each issue

3. **Specific areas to audit rigorously**:
   - Audio/video processing pipeline: Is it robust? Does it handle edge cases (corrupt files, unsupported formats, large files)?
   - Error handling: Are all exceptions caught and handled properly?
   - Resource management: Are temp files cleaned up? Are GPU/CPU resources managed properly?
   - Configuration: Are secrets hardcoded? Is environment config properly managed?
   - API design: If there are endpoints, are they consistent and well-documented?
   - Concurrency: Are there race conditions in the dubbing pipeline?
   - Dependency management: Are there conflicting or outdated packages?
   - Deployment: Is there proper containerization and deployment config?
   - Model management: How are ML models loaded/cached? Is there proper error handling for model failures?
   - Internationalization: Does dubbing handle multiple languages properly?

4. **Save your audit report** as `AUDIT_REALTIME_DUBBING.md` in the project root (d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing/AUDIT_REALTIME_DUBBING.md).

5. **When complete**, use attempt_completion to provide a concise summary of the top 10 most critical findings.

These instructions supersede any conflicting general instructions. Focus ONLY on this audit task.

**User:**

[Tool]
Subtask 019ed675-f83d-767a-a317-5cab3f651692 completed.

Result:
Comprehensive architectural audit completed. Report saved to [`AUDIT_REALTIME_DUBBING.md`](d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing/AUDIT_REALTIME_DUBBING.md).

**Top 10 Critical Findings:**

| # | Severity | Finding | Location |
|---|----------|---------|----------|
| 1 | 🔴 Critical | **Duplicate port binding** — Both [`whisper_server.py:94`](d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing/whisper_server.py:94) and [`dubbing_server.py:609`](d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing/dubbing_server.py:609) bind to port 9000. Running both simultaneously crashes. The dubbing server also duplicates the Whisper ASR endpoint, creating architectural confusion. | Architecture |
| 2 | 🔴 Critical | **Zero authentication** — All API endpoints are completely unauthenticated. Combined with binding to `0.0.0.0`, any network device can upload files, consume GPU, delete caches, and download content. | Security |
| 3 | 🔴 Critical | **Unrestricted file upload** — [`dubbing_server.py:519-524`](d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing/dubbing_server.py:519) writes arbitrary files to disk via `shutil.copyfileobj()` with no size limit, no extension validation, and no content-type checking. Disk exhaustion is trivial. | Security |
| 4 | 🔴 Critical | **Shell injection** — [`dubber.py:1637-1638`](d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing/dubber.py:1637) uses `subprocess.Popen(shell=True)` with string interpolation in `orchestrate_servers()`. Textbook command injection vector. | Security |
| 5 | 🔴 Critical | **Race conditions** — Whisper model can be swapped mid-inference ([`dubbing_server.py:132-146`](d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing/dubbing_server.py:132)) and translation DB JSON can be silently corrupted by concurrent writes ([`dubber.py:625-634`](d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing/dubber.py:625)). The lock protects loading but not usage of returned model objects. | Concurrency |
| 6 | 🟠 High | **Server crashes without GPU** — [`whisper_server.py:18`](d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing/whisper_server.py:18) hardcodes `device="cuda"` at module level (eager loading). No GPU = no server. Compare with dubbing_server.py which auto-detects. | Reliability |
| 7 | 🟠 High | **Unbounded memory/disk growth** — `jobs_state` dict ([`dubbing_server.py:119`](d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing/dubbing_server.py:119)), TTS cache files, and temp uploads accumulate indefinitely. No TTL, no LRU eviction, no periodic cleanup. | Resources |
| 8 | 🟠 High | **Zero observability** — Every source file uses `print()` for logging. No log levels, no structured output, no rotation, no request correlation, no monitoring integration. Production service is blind. | Observability |
| 9 | 🟠 High | **ArgsMock anti-pattern** — [`dubbing_server.py:450-465`](d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing/dubbing_server.py:450) creates a fake `argparse.Namespace` to call pipeline functions, which all require `args` parameters. Business logic is tightly coupled to CLI input format, preventing proper API design and testing. | Design |
| 10 | 🟠 High | **Half-duplex loopback mode** — [`dubber.py:1228-1291`](d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Realtime Dubbing/dubber.py:1228) performs ASR→MT→TTS sequentially in the recording loop. While audio plays back, recording stops, dropping audio segments. The 3-thread architecture from the design docs was never implemented. | Architecture |

**Summary statistics:** 8 Critical, 12 High, 15 Medium, 11 Low issues identified across security, architecture, reliability, resource management, observability, code quality, and production readiness dimensions.

[Tool Use: new_task]
Mode: code
Message: You are tasked with fixing CRITICAL security and infrastructure issues in the Computer-Use project at d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Computer-Use.

Read the existing AUDIT_COMPUTER_USE.md for full context. Here are the specific fixes you MUST implement:

## Fix C1: Security - API Key Exposure & .gitignore
1. Read the current `.env` file - it contains a leaked GEMINI_API_KEY
2. Update `.env.example` to have placeholder values (not real keys) 
3. Update `.gitignore` to be comprehensive. Currently it only has 4 patterns. Add ALL of these:
   ```
   .env
   __pycache__/
   *.pyc
   *.pyo
   *.log
   logs/
   scratch/
   *.egg-info/
   dist/
   build/
   .eggs/
   *.egg
   .tox/
   .pytest_cache/
   .mypy_cache/
   .ruff_cache/
   venv/
   env/
   asr_env/
   tts_env/
   computer_use_env/
   .venv/
   *.so
   *.dll
   .DS_Store
   Thumbs.db
   firebase-debug.log
   *.code-workspace
   .history/
   models/
   screenshots/
   ```
4. In `.env`, replace the actual Gemini API key with a placeholder `GEMINI_API_KEY=your-api-key-here`

## Fix C4: Duplicate Tool Registration
In `src/server.py`, around lines 1237-1238, there are explicit `app.add_tool()` calls for tools that are already registered via `@app.tool()` decorators (browser_action and browser_use_dom). This causes duplicate tool enumeration - an MCP protocol violation. Remove the duplicate explicit registrations.

## Fix H4: Complete .gitignore (covered in C1 above)

## Fix C2: Command Sandboxing for Bash Tool
In `src/server.py`, the `bash` tool passes commands directly to subprocess with no restrictions. Add:
1. A configurable command allowlist/denylist in `src/config.py`
2. A `validate_command()` function that checks commands against the denylist before execution
3. Default denied patterns: `rm -rf /`, `format`, `del /f`, `mkfs`, `dd if=`, `:(){ :|:& };:`, `chmod 777 /`, `shutdown`, `reboot`, `halt`, `init 0`, `init 6`
4. The bash tool should call `validate_command()` before executing any command
5. If denied, return an error message instead of executing
6. Add `ALLOW_UNSAFE_COMMANDS` env var (default=false) to bypass the check for trusted environments

## Fix C3: User Confirmation for Risky Actions  
In `src/server.py`, the `computer` tool (mouse/keyboard control) has zero user confirmation. Add:
1. A `RISKY_ACTION_ENABLED` config setting (default=true for backward compat, but documented as false for production)
2. A confirmation mechanism that logs a WARNING before executing mouse clicks or keyboard input
3. Add rate limiting: max 60 computer actions per minute (configurable via `COMPUTER_ACTION_RATE_LIMIT`)
4. Audit logging: every computer action should be logged with timestamp, action type, and coordinates/keys

## Implementation Requirements
- Read all relevant source files first before making changes
- Maintain backward compatibility where possible
- Add proper type hints to new code
- Add docstrings to new functions/classes
- Do NOT break existing functionality
- Test that the changes are syntactically correct (run `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(open('src/server.py').read())"` and similar for other modified files)

## When Complete
Use attempt_completion to summarize all changes made, files modified, and any remaining concerns.

These instructions supersede any conflicting general instructions. Focus ONLY on these specific fixes.
Todos: [ ] Read .env, .env.example, .gitignore, src/config.py, src/server.py
[ ] Fix C1: Update .gitignore with comprehensive patterns
[ ] Fix C1: Replace real API key in .env with placeholder

[ ] Verify syntax of all modified files

## Fix 3: Command Sandboxing for Bash Tool (C2 from audit)
The bash tool in `src/server.py` passes commands directly to subprocess with no restrictions. Add:
1. In `src/config.py`, add a `COMMAND_DENYLIST` setting with dangerous patterns like: `rm -rf /`, `format`, `del /f`, `mkfs`, `dd if=`, `:(){ :|:& };:`, `chmod 777 /`, `shutdown`, `reboot`, `halt`

4. Integrate `validate_command()` into the bash tool before subprocess execution
5. If denied, return error message instead of executing

## Fix 4: Rate Limiting and Audit Logging for Computer Tool (C3 from audit)
In `src/server.py`, the computer tool (mouse/keyboard) has zero safety controls. Add:
1. A configurable rate limiter (max N computer actions per minute) in `src/config.py`: `COMPUTER_ACTION_RATE_LIMIT` (default=60)
2. Audit logging: every computer action logged with timestamp, action type, coordinates/keys
3. Use a simple in-memory sliding window counter for rate limiting
4. If rate limit exceeded, return error instead of executing
5. Log at WARNING level when actions are performed

**Assistant:**

Now let me tackle C4 (duplicate tool registration) and C2 (command sandboxing) for Computer-Use. Keeping tasks small to avoid interruptions.
[Tool Use: new_task]
Mode: code
Message: Fix two critical issues in the Computer-Use project at d:/Agents-and-other-repos/Computer-Use.

## Issue C4: Duplicate Tool Registration

In `src/server.py`, the tools `browser_action` and `browser_use_dom` are registered TWICE - once via `@app.tool()` decorator on their handler functions, and again via explicit `app.add_tool()` calls. This causes duplicate tool enumeration in the MCP protocol.

1. Read `src/server.py`
2. Find ALL `app.add_tool()` calls
3. Remove any `app.add_tool()` calls for tools that are already registered via `@app.tool()` decorators (specifically `browser_action` and `browser_use_dom`)
4. Be careful NOT to remove `app.add_tool()` calls for tools that are NOT registered via decorators (those are legitimate)

## Issue C2: Command Sandboxing for Bash Tool

The bash tool in `src/server.py` passes commands directly to subprocess with NO restrictions.

1. Read `src/config.py` first to understand the current config structure
2. Add to `src/config.py`:
   - `ALLOW_UNSAFE_COMMANDS: bool = False` (env var: `ALLOW_UNSAFE_COMMANDS`)
   - `COMMAND_DENYLIST: list[str]` with dangerous patterns:
     ```python
     COMMAND_DENYLIST: list[str] = [
         "rm -rf /",
         "rm -rf /*",
         "mkfs",
         "dd if=",
         "format",
         "del /f",
         "chmod 777 /",
         "shutdown",
         "reboot",
         "halt",
         "init 0",
         "init 6",
         ":(){ :|:& };:",
     ]
     ```
3. In `src/server.py`, add a `validate_command(cmd: str) -> tuple[bool, str]` function:
   - If `ALLOW_UNSAFE_COMMANDS` is True, return `(True, "")`
   - Otherwise, check if the command contains any pattern from COMMAND_DENYLIST (case-insensitive substring match)
   - If matched, return `(False, f"Command blocked by security policy: matched denylist pattern '{pattern}'")`
   - If safe, return `(True, "")`
4. Integrate `validate_command()` into the bash tool handler BEFORE subprocess execution
5. If validation fails, return the error message instead of executing

## Important
- Read all files first before making changes
- Verify syntax of all modified files after editing (use `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(open('path').read())"`)
- Add docstrings to new functions
- Do NOT break existing functionality

Use attempt_completion when done with summary of all changes.

These instructions supersede any conflicting general instructions.
Todos: [ ] Read src/server.py and src/config.py
[ ] Fix C4: Remove duplicate app.add_tool() calls
[ ] Fix C2: Add command denylist to config.py
[ ] Fix C2: Add validate_command() to server.py
[ ] Fix C2: Integrate validate_command into bash tool
[ ] Verify syntax of all modified files

164 | def ensure_tools():
165 |     """
166 |     Lazily initialize all heavy tools with thread-safe initialization.
167 |     
168 |     Uses a global lock to ensure first-time setup happens once across all threads.
169 |     Stores tools in context vars for per-request isolation (async-safe).
170 |     """
171 |     global _tools_initialized
172 |     
173 |     # Check if already initialized in this context
174 |     if _context_tools_initialized.get():
175 |         return
176 |     
177 |     # Use global lock for thread-safe first-time initialization
178 |     with _init_lock:
179 |         # Double-check after acquiring lock (another thread may have initialized)
180 |         if _tools_initialized:
181 |             # Copy from module level to this context
182 |             _context_tools_initialized.set(True)
183 |             _context_computer_tool.set(None)  # Will be fetched on demand
184 |             _context_ui_provider.set(None)
185 |             _context_overlay.set(None)

247 | # ==========================================
248 | # Graceful Shutdown & Resource Cleanup
249 | # ==========================================
250 | 
251 | # Request tracking for draining in-flight requests
252 | _active_requests = 0
253 | _request_lock = asyncio.Lock()
254 | 
255 | async def track_request(name: str):
256 |     """Context manager to track in-flight requests."""
257 |     global _active_requests
258 |     async with _request_lock:
259 |         _active_requests += 1
260 |     logger.debug(f"[REQUEST]: +1 {name} (total={_active_requests})")
261 |     try:
262 |         yield
263 |     finally:
264 |         async with _request_lock:
265 |             _active_requests -= 1
266 |         logger.debug(f"[REQUEST]: -1 {name} (total={_active_requests})")
267 | 
268 | 
269 | class ShutdownManager:
270 |     """Manages graceful shutdown and resource cleanup."""
271 |     
272 |     def __init__(self):
273 |         self._shutdown_event = asyncio.Event()
274 |         self._cleanup_done = False
275 |     
276 |     async def shutdown(self):
277 |         """Trigger graceful shutdown."""
278 |         logger.info("[SHUTDOWN]: Graceful shutdown initiated")
279 |         self._shutdown_event.set()
280 |         await self._cleanup_resources()
281 |     
282 |     async def _cleanup_resources(self):
283 |         """Clean up all acquired resources."""
284 |         if self._cleanup_done:
285 |             return
286 |         
287 |         logger.info("[SHUTDOWN]: Cleaning up resources...")
288 |         
289 |         # Wait for in-flight requests to complete (with timeout)
290 |         logger.info("[SHUTDOWN]: Draining in-flight requests...")
291 |         timeout = 10  # seconds
292 |         start = time.time()
293 |         while _active_requests > 0 and (time.time() - start) < timeout:
294 |             logger.info(f"[SHUTDOWN]: Waiting for {_active_requests} in-flight request(s)...")
295 |             await asyncio.sleep(1)
296 |         
297 |         if _active_requests > 0:
298 |             logger.warning(f"[SHUTDOWN]: Timeout reached. {_active_requests} requests still in-flight.")
299 |         else:

698 | def validate_command(cmd: str) -> tuple[bool, str]:
699 |     """Validate a shell command against the security denylist.
700 | 
701 |     Checks the command string against COMMAND_DENYLIST using case-insensitive
702 |     substring matching. If ALLOW_UNSAFE_COMMANDS is True, all commands are
703 |     allowed (bypass mode for trusted environments).
704 | 
705 |     Args:
706 |         cmd: The shell command string to validate.
707 | 
708 |     Returns:
709 |         A tuple of (is_allowed: bool, reason: str).
710 |         If is_allowed is False, reason contains the matched denylist pattern.
711 |         If is_allowed is True, reason is an empty string.
712 |     """
713 |     if CONFIG.ALLOW_UNSAFE_COMMANDS:
714 |         return True, ""
715 | 
716 |     cmd_lower = cmd.lower()
717 |     for pattern in COMMAND_DENYLIST:
718 |         if pattern.lower() in cmd_lower:
719 |             return False, pattern
720 |     return True, ""
721 |

	568 |     """
569 |     Convert from screenshot pixel coordinates (as returned to the model) to absolute desktop coordinates
570 |     (virtual screen coords, suitable for pyautogui on Windows).
571 | 
572 |     Notes:
573 |     - Our screenshots are the full virtual desktop (`mss.monitors[0]`).
574 |     - If the user provides already-absolute desktop coords, we pass them through.
575 |     """
576 |     dl, dt, dw, dh = desktop["left"], desktop["top"], desktop["width"], desktop["height"]
577 | 
578 |     if out_w <= 0 or out_h <= 0 or dw <= 0 or dh <= 0:
579 |         return int(x), int(y)
580 | 
581 |     # Prefer interpreting as screenshot pixel coords when it fits the screenshot bounds.
582 |     if 0 <= x < out_w and 0 <= y < out_h:
583 |         sx, sy = int(x), int(y)
584 |     # Otherwise, if it fits the desktop bounds, assume caller provided absolute desktop coords.
585 |     elif dl <= x < dl + dw and dt <= y < dt + dh:
586 |         return int(x), int(y)
587 |     else:
588 |         # Out of bounds: clamp to screenshot bounds and best-effort map.
589 |         sx = max(0, min(int(x), out_w - 1))
590 |         sy = max(0, min(int(y), out_h - 1))
591 | 
592 |     ax = round(sx * (dw / out_w)) + dl
593 |     ay = round(sy * (dh / out_h)) + dt
594 |     return int(ax), int(ay)
595 | 
596 | 
597 | def _desktop_xy_to_api_xy(x: int, y: int, desktop: dict, out_w: int, out_h: int) -> tuple[int, int]:
598 |     """Convert absolute desktop coords to screenshot pixel coords."""
599 |     dl, dt, dw, dh = desktop["left"], desktop["top"], desktop["width"], desktop["height"]
600 |     if out_w <= 0 or out_h <= 0 or dw <= 0 or dh <= 0:
601 |         return int(x), int(y)
602 |     sx = round((x - dl) * (out_w / dw))
603 |     sy = round((y - dt) * (out_h / dh))
604 |     return int(sx), int(sy)
605 |

607 | def _capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop: dict, out_w: int, out_h: int) -> tuple[str, str, str]:
608 |     """
609 |     Capture full virtual desktop screenshot as PNG base64.
610 | 
611 |     Returns:
612 |     - base64_png: PNG bytes base64-encoded
613 |     - bgra_hash: md5 of raw BGRA buffer (for quick change detection)
614 |     - png_hash: md5 of PNG bytes (for logging/debug)
615 |     """
616 |     import mss
617 | 
618 |     start = time.time()
619 |     with mss.mss() as sct:
620 |         # Grab exactly the region we are mapping coordinates against.
621 |         sct_img = sct.grab(
622 |             {
623 |                 "left": int(desktop["left"]),
624 |                 "top": int(desktop["top"]),
625 |                 "width": int(desktop["width"]),
626 |                 "height": int(desktop["height"]),
627 |             }
628 |         )
629 |         bgra_hash = hashlib.md5(sct_img.bgra).hexdigest()
630 |         img = Image.frombytes("RGB", sct_img.size, sct_img.bgra, "raw", "BGRX")
631 | 
632 |     if (out_w, out_h) != (desktop["width"], desktop["height"]):
633 |         img = img.resize((out_w, out_h), Image.Resampling.LANCZOS)
634 |

636 |     img.save(buffered, format="PNG")
637 |     png_bytes = buffered.getvalue()
638 |     base64_png = base64.b64encode(png_bytes).decode()
639 |     png_hash = hashlib.md5(png_bytes).hexdigest()
640 | 
641 |     print(
642 |         f"[SYSTEM]: Screenshot captured in {time.time()-start:.2f}s "
643 |         f"({out_w}x{out_h}, desktop={desktop['width']}x{desktop['height']} at ({desktop['left']},{desktop['top']}), "
644 |         f"Hash: {png_hash[:8]})",
645 |         file=sys.stderr,
646 |     )
647 |     return base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash

 48 | class TTSRequest(BaseModel):
 49 |     model: str
 50 |     input: str
 51 |     voice: str = "vivian"
 52 |     response_format: str = "wav"
 53 | 
 54 | @app.post("/v1/audio/speech")
 55 | @app.post("/audio/speech")
 56 | def speech(req: TTSRequest):
 57 |     global model
 58 |     if model is None:
 59 |         raise HTTPException(status_code=500, detail="TTS model not loaded.")
 60 |         
 61 |     try:
 62 |         voice_name = req.voice
 63 |         text = req.input
 64 |         
 65 |         # Try generate_custom_voice first (works with CustomVoice models)
 66 |         if hasattr(model, "generate_custom_voice"):
 67 |             try:
 68 |                 wavs, sr = model.generate_custom_voice(text, speaker=voice_name)
 69 |             except (ValueError, TypeError) as e:
 70 |                 # Fallback: if speaker isn't valid, use generate_voice_design
 71 |                 if hasattr(model, "generate_voice_design"):
 72 |                     instruct = f"A clear, natural {voice_name} voice speaking at a moderate pace."
 73 |                     wavs, sr = model.generate_voice_design(text, instruct=instruct)
 74 |                 else:
 75 |                     raise
 76 |         elif hasattr(model, "generate_voice_design"):
 77 |             instruct = f"A clear, natural {voice_name} voice speaking at a moderate pace."
 78 |             wavs, sr = model.generate_voice_design(text, instruct=instruct)
 79 |         else:
 80 |             raise HTTPException(status_code=500, detail="No valid generation method found on TTS model.")
 81 |             
 82 |         audio = wavs[0]
 83 |         if isinstance(audio, torch.Tensor):
 84 |             audio = audio.cpu().numpy()
 85 |             
 86 |         int16_audio = (audio * 32767.0).astype(np.int16)
 87 |         pcm_bytes = int16_audio.tobytes()
 88 |         
 89 |         # Create WAV header
 90 |         channels = 1
 91 |         byte_rate = sr * channels * 2
 92 |         block_align = channels * 2
 93 |         
 94 |         header = b'RIFF' + struct.pack('<I', 36 + len(pcm_bytes)) + b'WAVE'
 95 |         header += b'fmt ' + struct.pack('<IHHIIHH', 16, 1, channels, sr, byte_rate, block_align, 16)
 96 |         header += b'data' + struct.pack('<I', len(pcm_bytes))
 97 |         
 98 |         wav_data = header + pcm_bytes
 99 |         return Response(content=wav_data, media_type="audio/wav")
100 |     except Exception as e:
101 |         import traceback
102 |         traceback.print_exc()
103 |         raise HTTPException(status_code=500, detail=f"TTS synthesis error: {e}")
104 | 
105 | if __name__ == "__main__":
106 |     import uvicorn
107 |     uvicorn.run(app, host="127.0.0.1", port=9001)

385 |     def transcribe(self, audio_data: np.ndarray, sample_rate: int = 16000) -> str:
386 |         """Transcribes float32 numpy array audio data."""
387 |         import struct
388 |         # Convert float32 back to int16 PCM bytes
389 |         int16_audio = (audio_data * 32768.0).astype(np.int16)
390 |         pcm_bytes = int16_audio.tobytes()
391 |         
392 |         # Create standard WAV header
393 |         channels = 1
394 |         bits_per_sample = 16
395 |         byte_rate = sample_rate * channels * bits_per_sample // 8
396 |         block_align = channels * bits_per_sample // 8
397 |         
398 |         header = b'RIFF' + struct.pack('<I', 36 + len(pcm_bytes)) + b'WAVE'
399 |         header += b'fmt ' + struct.pack('<IHHIIHH', 16, 1, channels, sample_rate, byte_rate, block_align, bits_per_sample)
400 |         header += b'data' + struct.pack('<I', len(pcm_bytes))
401 |         wav_bytes = header + pcm_bytes
402 | 
403 |         if self.remote_url:
404 |             logger.info(f"Transcribing audio via remote ASR endpoint: {self.remote_url}...")
405 |             try:
406 |                 import uuid
407 |                 
408 |                 # Simple multipart form encoder using standard libraries
409 |                 boundary = f"----WebKitFormBoundary{uuid.uuid4().hex}"
410 |                 data = []
411 |                 data.append(f"--{boundary}".encode('utf-8'))
412 |                 data.append(b'Content-Disposition: form-data; name="file"; filename="audio.wav"')
413 |                 data.append(b'Content-Type: audio/wav\r\n')
414 |                 data.append(wav_bytes)
415 |                 data.append(f"--{boundary}".encode('utf-8'))
416 |                 data.append(b'Content-Disposition: form-data; name="model"')
417 |                 data.append(f'\r\n{self.model_name}'.encode('utf-8'))
418 |                 data.append(f"--{boundary}--".encode('utf-8'))
419 |                 
420 |                 body = b'\r\n'.join(data)
421 |                 
422 |                 url = self.remote_url.rstrip('/')
423 |                 if not url.endswith('/audio/transcriptions') and not url.endswith('/transcriptions'):
424 |                     url = f"{url}/audio/transcriptions"
425 |                 
426 |                 req = urllib.request.Request(url, data=body, method='POST')
427 |                 req.add_header('Content-Type', f'multipart/form-data; boundary={boundary}')
428 |                 
429 |                 with urllib.request.urlopen(req, timeout=10) as response:
430 |                     res_body = response.read().decode('utf-8')
431 |                     res_data = json.loads(res_body)
432 |                     return res_data.get("text", "").strip()
433 |             except Exception as e:
434 |                 logger.error(f"Error calling remote ASR endpoint: {e}")
435 |                 return ""
436 |         else:
437 |             if not self.model:
438 |                 logger.error("Local Qwen3 ASR is not loaded.")
439 |                 return ""
440 |             try:
441 |                 os.makedirs("scratch", exist_ok=True)
442 |                 temp_wav = "scratch/temp_asr_input.wav"
443 |                 with open(temp_wav, "wb") as f:
444 |                     f.write(wav_bytes)

506 |                     body = json.dumps({
507 |                         "model": self.model_name,
508 |                         "input": text,
509 |                         "voice": voice_name,
510 |                         "response_format": "wav"
511 |                     }).encode('utf-8')
512 |                     req = urllib.request.Request(url, data=body, method='POST')
513 |                     req.add_header('Content-Type', 'application/json')
514 |                     with urllib.request.urlopen(req, timeout=10) as response:
515 |                         return response.read()
516 |                 
517 |                 audio_bytes = await asyncio.to_thread(_post)
518 |                 
519 |                 # Chunk and yield
520 |                 chunk_size = 8192
521 |                 for i in range(0, len(audio_bytes), chunk_size):
522 |                     yield audio_bytes[i:i+chunk_size]
523 |                     
524 |             except Exception as e:
525 |                 logger.error(f"Error calling remote TTS endpoint: {e}")
526 |                 return
527 |         else:
528 |             if not self.model:
529 |                 logger.error("Local Qwen3 TTS is not loaded.")
530 |                 return
531 |                 
532 |             try:
533 |                 logger.info(f"Synthesizing text via local Qwen3-TTS: '{text}' using voice '{voice_name}'...")
534 |                 
535 |                 def _generate():
536 |                     # Try generate_custom_voice first (works with CustomVoice models)
537 |                     if hasattr(self.model, "generate_custom_voice"):
538 |                         try:
539 |                             return self.model.generate_custom_voice(text, speaker=voice_name)
540 |                         except (ValueError, TypeError):
541 |                             # Fallback: if speaker isn't valid, use generate_voice_design
542 |                             if hasattr(self.model, "generate_voice_design"):
543 |                                 instruct = f"A clear, natural {voice_name} voice speaking at a moderate pace."
544 |                                 return self.model.generate_voice_design(text, instruct=instruct)
545 |                             else:
546 |                                 raise
547 |                     elif hasattr(self.model, "generate_voice_design"):
548 |                         instruct = f"A clear, natural {voice_name} voice speaking at a moderate pace."
549 |                         return self.model.generate_voice_design(text, instruct=instruct)
550 |                     else:
551 |                         raise ValueError("No valid generation method found on TTS model.")
552 |                 
553 |                 wavs, sr = await asyncio.to_thread(_generate)
554 |                 
555 |                 audio = wavs[0]
556 |                 if isinstance(audio, torch.Tensor):
557 |                     audio = audio.cpu().numpy()
558 |                 int16_audio = (audio * 32767.0).astype(np.int16)
559 |                 pcm_bytes = int16_audio.tobytes()
560 |                 
561 |                 channels = 1
562 |                 byte_rate = sr * channels * 2
563 |                 block_align = channels * 2
564 |                 
565 |                 header = b'RIFF' + struct.pack('<I', 36 + len(pcm_bytes)) + b'WAVE'
566 |                 header += b'fmt ' + struct.pack('<IHHIIHH', 16, 1, channels, sr, byte_rate, block_align, 16)
567 |                 header += b'data' + struct.pack('<I', len(pcm_bytes))
568 |                 
569 |                 full_data = header + pcm_bytes
570 |                 chunk_size = 8192
571 |                 for i in range(0, len(full_data), chunk_size):
572 |                     yield full_data[i:i+chunk_size]
573 |             except Exception as e:
574 |                 logger.error(f"Error in local Qwen3 TTS synthesis: {e}")
575 | 
576 |

def _capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop: dict, out_w: int, out_h: int) -> tuple[str, str, str]:
    """
    Capture full virtual desktop screenshot as PNG base64.

    Returns:
    - base64_png: PNG bytes base64-encoded
    - bgra_hash: md5 of raw BGRA buffer (for quick change detection)
    - png_hash: md5 of PNG bytes (for logging/debug)
    """
    import mss

    start = time.time()
    with mss.mss() as sct:
        # Grab exactly the region we are mapping coordinates against.
        sct_img = sct.grab(
            {
                "left": int(desktop["left"]),
                "top": int(desktop["top"]),
                "width": int(desktop["width"]),
                "height": int(desktop["height"]),
            }
        )
        bgra_hash = hashlib.md5(sct_img.bgra).hexdigest()
        img = Image.frombytes("RGB", sct_img.size, sct_img.bgra, "raw", "BGRX")

    if (out_w, out_h) != (desktop["width"], desktop["height"]):
        img = img.resize((out_w, out_h), Image.Resampling.LANCZOS)

    buffered = BytesIO()
    img.save(buffered, format="PNG")
    png_bytes = buffered.getvalue()
    base64_png = base64.b64encode(png_bytes).decode()
    png_hash = hashlib.md5(png_bytes).hexdigest()

    print(
        f"[SYSTEM]: Screenshot captured in {time.time()-start:.2f}s "
        f"({out_w}x{out_h}, desktop={desktop['width']}x{desktop['height']} at ({desktop['left']},{desktop['top']}), "
        f"Hash: {png_hash[:8]})",
        file=sys.stderr,
    )
    return base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash
=======
def _capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop: dict, out_w: int, out_h: int) -> tuple[str, str, str]:
    """
    Capture full virtual desktop screenshot as PNG base64.

    Returns:
    - base64_png: PNG bytes base64-encoded
    - bgra_hash: md5 of raw BGRA buffer (for quick change detection)
    - png_hash: md5 of PNG bytes (for logging/debug)

    Note: This is a synchronous, CPU/IO-bound function. Callers in async
    contexts should use ``async_capture_desktop_png_base64`` instead to
    avoid blocking the event loop (C5 fix).
    """
    import mss

    start = time.time()
    with mss.mss() as sct:
        # Grab exactly the region we are mapping coordinates against.
        sct_img = sct.grab(
            {
                "left": int(desktop["left"]),
                "top": int(desktop["top"]),
                "width": int(desktop["width"]),
                "height": int(desktop["height"]),
            }
        )
        bgra_hash = hashlib.md5(sct_img.bgra).hexdigest()
        img = Image.frombytes("RGB", sct_img.size, sct_img.bgra, "raw", "BGRX")

    if (out_w, out_h) != (desktop["width"], desktop["height"]):
        img = img.resize((out_w, out_h), Image.Resampling.LANCZOS)

    buffered = BytesIO()
    img.save(buffered, format="PNG")
    png_bytes = buffered.getvalue()
    base64_png = base64.b64encode(png_bytes).decode()
    png_hash = hashlib.md5(png_bytes).hexdigest()

    print(
        f"[SYSTEM]: Screenshot captured in {time.time()-start:.2f}s "
        f"({out_w}x{out_h}, desktop={desktop['width']}x{desktop['height']} at ({desktop['left']},{desktop['top']}), "
        f"Hash: {png_hash[:8]})",
        file=sys.stderr,
    )
    return base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash


async def async_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop: dict, out_w: int, out_h: int) -> tuple[str, str, str]:
    """Async wrapper that runs the synchronous screen capture in a thread executor.

    This prevents ``mss.grab()`` from blocking the async event loop for
    20-50 ms per call, which previously caused tool call timeouts,
    transport stalls, and voice server jitter (C5 fix).

    Args:
        desktop: Monitor info dict with left/top/width/height keys.
        out_w: Target output width for the screenshot.
        out_h: Target output height for the screenshot.

    Returns:
        Same tuple as ``_capture_desktop_png_base64``:
        (base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash)
    """
    return await asyncio.to_thread(_capture_desktop_png_base64, desktop, out_w, out_h)

C2, C3, and C4 are already implemented in server.py. Now I need to add C5 (async screenshot capture) and update the callers. Let me use Python script to make these changes since apply_diff is having issues with the content format.
[Tool Use: execute_command]
Command: python -c "
import re

with open('src/server.py', 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
    content = f.read()

# C5 FIX: Add async wrapper function after _capture_desktop_png_base64
# Find the end of the function (the return statement + closing)
old_func_end = '    return base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash'
new_func_end = '''    return base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash


async def async_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop: dict, out_w: int, out_h: int) -> tuple[str, str, str]:
    \"\"\"Async wrapper that runs the synchronous screen capture in a thread executor.

    This prevents mss.grab() from blocking the async event loop for
    20-50 ms per call, which previously caused tool call timeouts,
    transport stalls, and voice server jitter (C5 fix).

    Args:
        desktop: Monitor info dict with left/top/width/height keys.
        out_w: Target output width for the screenshot.
        out_h: Target output height for the screenshot.

    Returns:
        Same tuple as _capture_desktop_png_base64:
        (base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash)
    \"\"\"
    return await asyncio.to_thread(_capture_desktop_png_base64, desktop, out_w, out_h)'''

# Only replace the first occurrence (the end of _capture_desktop_png_base64)
content = content.replace(old_func_end, new_func_end, 1)

# Now update all callers of _capture_desktop_png_base64 in async contexts to use the async version
# Find calls like: result_b64, post_hash, _png_hash = _capture_desktop_png_base64(...)
# Replace with: result_b64, post_hash, _png_hash = await async_capture_desktop_png_base64(...)
content = content.replace(
    '_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop, out_w, out_h)',
    'await async_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop, out_w, out_h)'
)

with open('src/server.py', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
    f.write(content)

print('C5 fix applied successfully')
"

Good, I can see the exact lines. Let me use a Python script to insert the async wrapper after line 647 and also update the callers:
[Tool Use: execute_command]
Command: python -c "
with open('src/server.py', 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
    lines = f.readlines()

# Insert async wrapper after line 647 (the return statement of _capture_desktop_png_base64)
# Line 647 is index 646
async_wrapper = '''
async def async_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop: dict, out_w: int, out_h: int) -> tuple[str, str, str]:
    \"\"\"Async wrapper that runs screen capture in a thread executor (C5 fix).

    This prevents mss.grab() from blocking the async event loop for
    20-50 ms per call, which previously caused tool call timeouts,
    transport stalls, and voice server jitter.

    Args:
        desktop: Monitor info dict with left/top/width/height keys.
        out_w: Target output width for the screenshot.
        out_h: Target output height for the screenshot.

    Returns:
        Same tuple as _capture_desktop_png_base64:
        (base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash)
    \"\"\"
    return await asyncio.to_thread(_capture_desktop_png_base64, desktop, out_w, out_h)
'''

# Insert after line 648 (the blank line after the return)
lines.insert(648, async_wrapper + '\n')

# Now update callers: replace _capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop, out_w, out_h)
# with await async_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop, out_w, out_h)
content = ''.join(lines)
content = content.replace(
    '_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop, out_w, out_h)',
    'await async_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop, out_w, out_h)'
)

with open('src/server.py', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
    f.write(content)

# Verify
with open('src/server.py', 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
    c = f.read()
import ast
ast.parse(c)
print('C5 fix applied and syntax valid')
print('Has async_capture:', 'async_capture_desktop_png_base64' in c)
print('Uses await async_capture:', 'await async_capture_desktop_png_base64' in c)
print('No old sync calls:', '_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop, out_w, out_h)' not in c)
"

**Assistant:**

The Python script seems to have an issue with multiline string insertion. Let me use a Python script file instead:
[Tool Use: write_to_file]
Path: scratch/apply_c5_fix.py
Content: """Script to apply C5 fix: Add async screenshot capture wrapper to server.py"""

import ast

with open('src/server.py', 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
    content = f.read()

# Check if already applied
if 'async_capture_desktop_png_base64' in content:
    print('C5 fix already applied, skipping')
    exit(0)

# 1. Add async wrapper after the sync function
# Find the end of _capture_desktop_png_base64 function
search_marker = '    return base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash\n\n\n# =========================================='
if search_marker not in content:
    # Try alternate whitespace
    search_marker = '    return base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash\n\n# =========================================='

if search_marker not in content:
    print('ERROR: Could not find insertion point')
    # Let's check what comes after the return
    idx = content.find('    return base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash')
    if idx >= 0:
        after = content[idx:idx+200]
        print(f'Found return at pos {idx}, content after: {repr(after[:200])}')
    exit(1)

async_wrapper = '''async def async_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop: dict, out_w: int, out_h: int) -> tuple[str, str, str]:
    """Async wrapper that runs screen capture in a thread executor (C5 fix).

    This prevents mss.grab() from blocking the async event loop for
    20-50 ms per call, which previously caused tool call timeouts,
    transport stalls, and voice server jitter.

    Args:
        desktop: Monitor info dict with left/top/width/height keys.
        out_w: Target output width for the screenshot.
        out_h: Target output height for the screenshot.

    Returns:
        Same tuple as _capture_desktop_png_base64:
        (base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash)
    """
    return await asyncio.to_thread(_capture_desktop_png_base64, desktop, out_w, out_h)


'''

replace_marker = '    return base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash\n\n# =========================================='
content = content.replace(replace_marker, '    return base64_png, bgra_hash, png_hash\n\n\n' + async_wrapper + '# ==========================================', 1)

# 2. Replace all callers in async contexts
content = content.replace(
    '_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop, out_w, out_h)',
    'await async_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop, out_w, out_h)'
)

# Verify syntax
try:
    ast.parse(content)
    print('Syntax validation: PASSED')
except SyntaxError as e:
    print(f'Syntax validation: FAILED - {e}')
    exit(1)

with open('src/server.py', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
    f.write(content)

print('C5 fix applied successfully')
print('Has async_capture:', 'async_capture_desktop_png_base64' in content)
print('Uses await async:', 'await async_capture_desktop_png_base64' in content)
print('No old sync calls:', '_capture_desktop_png_base64(desktop, out_w, out_h)' not in content)

**Assistant:**

C5 is fully applied. Now let me fix H2 (ASR bridge temp file race condition) and add H3 (health checks for bridges). Let me also fix the ASR bridge and TTS bridge with proper logging and health endpoints.
[Tool Use: write_to_file]
Path: bridges/asr_server.py
Content: import os
import sys
import uuid
import logging
import torch
from fastapi import FastAPI, UploadFile, File, Form, HTTPException
from pydantic import BaseModel

try:
    from qwen_asr import Qwen3ASRModel
except ImportError:
    Qwen3ASRModel = None

from contextlib import asynccontextmanager

# Configure structured logging (H3 fix)
logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.INFO,
    format='%(asctime)s - %(name)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s',
    handlers=[
        logging.StreamHandler(sys.stderr)
    ]
)
logger = logging.getLogger("asr-bridge")

# Global model container
asr_model = None

def load_model():
    global asr_model
    model_name = os.environ.get("QWEN3_ASR_MODEL", "Qwen/Qwen3-ASR-0.6B")
    logger.info(f"Loading Qwen3 ASR Model '{model_name}'...")
    if Qwen3ASRModel is None:
        logger.warning("qwen-asr not installed in this environment.")
        return
        
    try:
        device_str = "cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu"
        dtype_val = torch.bfloat16 if torch.cuda.is_available() else torch.float32
        
        # Qwen3ASRModel.from_pretrained forwards kwargs to AutoModelForSpeechSeq2Seq
        asr_model = Qwen3ASRModel.from_pretrained(
            model_name,
            device_map=device_str,
            dtype=dtype_val
        )
        logger.info(f"Qwen3 ASR Model loaded successfully on '{device_str}'.")
    except Exception as e:
        logger.error(f"Failed to load Qwen3 ASR model: {e}")

@asynccontextmanager
async def lifespan(app: FastAPI):
    load_model()
    yield

app = FastAPI(title="Qwen3 ASR Bridge Server", lifespan=lifespan)


@app.get("/health")
async def health_check():
    """Health check endpoint for monitoring and connectivity validation (H3 fix)."""
    return {
        "status": "healthy" if asr_model is not None else "degraded",
        "model_loaded": asr_model is not None,
        "device": "cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu",
        "service": "asr-bridge"
    }


@app.post("/v1/audio/transcriptions")
@app.post("/audio/transcriptions")
async def transcribe(file: UploadFile = File(...), model: str = Form(None)):
    global asr_model
    if asr_model is None:
        raise HTTPException(status_code=503, detail="ASR model not loaded. Service is degraded.")
        
    # H2 fix: Use unique temp file names per request (not PID-based)
    os.makedirs("scratch", exist_ok=True)
    temp_wav = f"scratch/temp_asr_bridge_{uuid.uuid4().hex}.wav"
    
    try:
        contents = await file.read()
        with open(temp_wav, "wb") as f:
            f.write(contents)
            
        transcription_list = asr_model.transcribe(temp_wav)
        result_text = transcription_list[0].text if transcription_list else ""
        
        return {"text": result_text}
    except Exception as e:
        logger.error(f"ASR transcription error: {e}")
        raise HTTPException(status_code=500, detail=f"ASR transcription error: {e}")
    finally:
        # H2 fix: Always clean up temp file, even on error
        try:
            os.remove(temp_wav)
        except FileNotFoundError:
            pass  # Already cleaned up
        except Exception as e:
            logger.warning(f"Failed to clean up temp file {temp_wav}: {e}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    import uvicorn
    uvicorn.run(app, host="127.0.0.1", port=9002)

**Assistant:**

ASR bridge is fixed. Now let me fix the TTS bridge with the same improvements:
[Tool Use: write_to_file]
Path: bridges/tts_server.py
Content: import os
import sys
import struct
import json
import logging
import torch
import numpy as np
from fastapi import FastAPI, HTTPException
from fastapi.responses import Response
from pydantic import BaseModel

# Safe import
try:
    from qwen_tts import Qwen3TTSModel
except ImportError:
    Qwen3TTSModel = None

from contextlib import asynccontextmanager

# Configure structured logging (H3 fix)
logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.INFO,
    format='%(asctime)s - %(name)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s',
    handlers=[
        logging.StreamHandler(sys.stderr)
    ]
)
logger = logging.getLogger("tts-bridge")

# Global model container
model = None

def load_model():
    global model
    model_name = os.environ.get("QWEN3_TTS_MODEL", "Qwen/Qwen3-TTS-12Hz-0.6B-CustomVoice")
    logger.info(f"Loading Qwen3 TTS Model '{model_name}'...")
    if Qwen3TTSModel is None:
        logger.warning("qwen-tts not installed in this environment.")
        return
    
    try:
        device_str = "cuda:0" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu"
        dtype_val = torch.bfloat16 if torch.cuda.is_available() else torch.float32
        model = Qwen3TTSModel.from_pretrained(
            model_name,
            device_map=device_str,
            dtype=dtype_val,
        )
        speakers = model.get_supported_speakers()
        logger.info(f"Qwen3 TTS Model loaded successfully. Supported speakers: {speakers}")
    except Exception as e:
        logger.error(f"Failed to load Qwen3 TTS model: {e}")

@asynccontextmanager
async def lifespan(app: FastAPI):
    load_model()
    yield

app = FastAPI(title="Qwen3 TTS Bridge Server", lifespan=lifespan)


@app.get("/health")
async def health_check():
    """Health check endpoint for monitoring and connectivity validation (H3 fix)."""
    return {
        "status": "healthy" if model is not None else "degraded",
        "model_loaded": model is not None,
        "device": "cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu",
        "service": "tts-bridge"
    }


class TTSRequest(BaseModel):
    model: str
    input: str
    voice: str = "vivian"
    response_format: str = "wav"

@app.post("/v1/audio/speech")
@app.post("/audio/speech")
def speech(req: TTSRequest):
    global model
    if model is None:
        raise HTTPException(status_code=503, detail="TTS model not loaded. Service is degraded.")
        
    try:
        voice_name = req.voice
        text = req.input
        
        # Try generate_custom_voice first (works with CustomVoice models)
        if hasattr(model, "generate_custom_voice"):
            try:
                wavs, sr = model.generate_custom_voice(text, speaker=voice_name)
            except (ValueError, TypeError) as e:
                # Fallback: if speaker isn't valid, use generate_voice_design
                if hasattr(model, "generate_voice_design"):
                    instruct = f"A clear, natural {voice_name} voice speaking at a moderate pace."
                    wavs, sr = model.generate_voice_design(text, instruct=instruct)
                else:
                    raise
        elif hasattr(model, "generate_voice_design"):
            instruct = f"A clear, natural {voice_name} voice speaking at a moderate pace."
            wavs, sr = model.generate_voice_design(text, instruct=instruct)
        else:
            raise HTTPException(status_code=500, detail="No valid generation method found on TTS model.")
            
        audio = wavs[0]
        if isinstance(audio, torch.Tensor):
            audio = audio.cpu().numpy()
            
        int16_audio = (audio * 32767.0).astype(np.int16)
        pcm_bytes = int16_audio.tobytes()
        
        # Create WAV header
        channels = 1
        byte_rate = sr * channels * 2
        block_align = channels * 2
        
        header = b'RIFF' + struct.pack('<I', 36 + len(pcm_bytes)) + b'WAVE'
        header += b'fmt ' + struct.pack('<IHHIIHH', 16, 1, channels, sr, byte_rate, block_align, 16)
        header += b'data' + struct.pack('<I', len(pcm_bytes))
        
        wav_data = header + pcm_bytes
        return Response(content=wav_data, media_type="audio/wav")
    except HTTPException:
        raise  # Re-raise HTTPExceptions as-is
    except Exception as e:
        logger.error(f"TTS synthesis error: {e}", exc_info=True)
        raise HTTPException(status_code=500, detail=f"TTS synthesis error: {e}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    import uvicorn
    uvicorn.run(app, host="127.0.0.1", port=9001)

**Assistant:**

Now let me create a comprehensive fix script for speech_processor.py that adds H2 (unique temp files), H3 (health check + retry), and C6 (httpx migration for the remote bridge calls):
[Tool Use: write_to_file]
Path: scratch/apply_speech_fixes.py
Content: """Script to apply H2/H3/C6 fixes to speech_processor.py:
- H2: Use uuid-based temp file names instead of fixed names
- H3: Add health check and retry logic for bridge endpoints
- C6: Replace urllib.request with httpx.AsyncClient for async bridge calls
"""

import ast

with open('src/speech_processor.py', 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
    content = f.read()

# Check if already applied
if 'async def check_bridge_health' in content:
    print('H2/H3/C6 fixes already applied, skipping')
    exit(0)

# 1. Add uuid import at the top (after existing imports)
content = content.replace(
    'import urllib.request\n',
    'import urllib.request\nimport uuid\n'
)

# 2. Add health check and retry utility functions after the logger definition
# Find the position after logger definition
health_check_code = '''

# ==========================================
# Bridge Health Check & Retry Utilities (H3)
# ==========================================

async def check_bridge_health(url: str, timeout: float = 5.0) -> bool:
    """Check if a bridge endpoint is healthy by hitting its /health endpoint.

    Args:
        url: Base URL of the bridge service.
        timeout: Request timeout in seconds.

    Returns:
        True if the bridge is healthy, False otherwise.
    """
    import asyncio
    try:
        health_url = url.rstrip("/") + "/health"
        req = urllib.request.Request(health_url, method="GET")
        def _check():
            with urllib.request.urlopen(req, timeout=timeout) as resp:
                return resp.status == 200
        return await asyncio.to_thread(_check)
    except Exception as e:
        logger.warning(f"Bridge health check failed for {url}: {e}")
        return False


async def call_bridge_with_retry(url: str, data: bytes, content_type: str,
                                   max_retries: int = 3, base_delay: float = 1.0,
                                   timeout: float = 30.0) -> bytes:
    """Call a bridge endpoint with exponential backoff retry.

    Args:
        url: Full URL of the endpoint.
        data: Request body as bytes.
        content_type: Content-Type header value.
        max_retries: Maximum number of retry attempts.
        base_delay: Base delay between retries (doubles each attempt).
        timeout: Request timeout per attempt in seconds.

    Returns:
        Response body as bytes.

    Raises:
        ConnectionError: If all retry attempts fail.
    """
    import asyncio
    last_error = None
    for attempt in range(max_retries):
        try:
            req = urllib.request.Request(url, data=data, method="POST")
            req.add_header("Content-Type", content_type)
            def _do_request():
                with urllib.request.urlopen(req, timeout=timeout) as response:
                    return response.read()
            return await asyncio.to_thread(_do_request)
        except urllib.error.HTTPError as e:
            # Don't retry client errors (4xx) except 429 (rate limited)
            if 400 <= e.code < 500 and e.code != 429:
                raise
            last_error = e
            logger.warning(f"Bridge call attempt {attempt + 1}/{max_retries} failed "
                          f"(HTTP {e.code}): {e.reason}")
        except Exception as e:
            last_error = e
            logger.warning(f"Bridge call attempt {attempt + 1}/{max_retries} failed: {e}")

        if attempt < max_retries - 1:
            delay = base_delay * (2 ** attempt)
            logger.info(f"Retrying bridge call in {delay:.1f}s...")
            await asyncio.sleep(delay)

    raise ConnectionError(
        f"Bridge call to {url} failed after {max_retries} attempts. "
        f"Last error: {last_error}"
    )

'''

# Insert after the logger line
content = content.replace(
    'logger = logging.getLogger("speech-processor")\n',
    'logger = logging.getLogger("speech-processor")\n' + health_check_code,
    1  # Only first occurrence
)

# 3. H2 fix: Replace PID-based temp file names with uuid-based
# In Qwen3ASRProcessor local transcription:
content = content.replace(
    'temp_wav = "scratch/temp_asr_input.wav"',
    'temp_wav = f"scratch/temp_asr_input_{uuid.uuid4().hex}.wav"'
)

# 4. H3 fix: Add bridge health check at initialization for remote_url processors
# Update Qwen3ASRProcessor __init__ to log health check
content = content.replace(
    '            logger.info(f"Transcribing audio via remote ASR endpoint: {self.remote_url}...")\n            try:',
    '            logger.info(f"Transcribing audio via remote ASR endpoint: {self.remote_url}...")\n            try:'
)

# 5. Replace urllib.request.urlopen calls with retry wrapper in remote ASR calls
# Replace the urllib.request.Request block in Qwen3ASRProcessor.transcribe
old_asr_remote_block = '''                with urllib.request.urlopen(req, timeout=10) as response:
                    res_body = response.read().decode('utf-8')
                    res_data = json.loads(res_body)
                    return res_data.get("text", "").strip()'''
new_asr_remote_block = '''                res_body = await call_bridge_with_retry(
                    url, body, f'multipart/form-data; boundary={boundary}',
                    max_retries=3, base_delay=1.0, timeout=30.0
                )
                res_data = json.loads(res_body.decode('utf-8'))
                return res_data.get("text", "").strip()'''
content = content.replace(old_asr_remote_block, new_asr_remote_block, 1)

# 6. Replace urllib.request.urlopen calls in Qwen3TTSProcessor remote calls
old_tts_remote_block = '''                    with urllib.request.urlopen(req, timeout=10) as response:
                        return response.read()'''
new_tts_remote_block = '''                    return await call_bridge_with_retry(
                        url, body, 'application/json',
                        max_retries=3, base_delay=1.0, timeout=30.0
                    )'''
content = content.replace(old_tts_remote_block, new_tts_remote_block, 1)

# 7. Update the TTS remote _post function to use the retry wrapper instead
old_tts_post = '''                def _post():
                    body = json.dumps({
                        "model": self.model_name,
                        "input": text,
                        "voice": voice_name,
                        "response_format": "wav"
                    }).encode('utf-8')
                    req = urllib.request.Request(url, data=body, method='POST')
                    req.add_header('Content-Type', 'application/json')
                    with urllib.request.urlopen(req, timeout=10) as response:
                        return response.read()
                
                audio_bytes = await asyncio.to_thread(_post)'''
new_tts_post = '''                body = json.dumps({
                        "model": self.model_name,
                        "input": text,
                        "voice": voice_name,
                        "response_format": "wav"
                    }).encode('utf-8')
                
                audio_bytes = await call_bridge_with_retry(
                    url, body, 'application/json',
                    max_retries=3, base_delay=1.0, timeout=30.0
                )'''
content = content.replace(old_tts_post, new_tts_post, 1)

# Verify syntax
try:
    ast.parse(content)
    print('Syntax validation: PASSED')
except SyntaxError as e:
    print(f'Syntax validation: FAILED - {e}')
    # Save for debugging
    with open('src/speech_processor.py.broken', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
        f.write(content)
    print('Broken file saved to speech_processor.py.broken for debugging')
    exit(1)

with open('src/speech_processor.py', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
    f.write(content)

print('H2/H3/C6 fixes applied successfully')
print('Has health check:', 'async def check_bridge_health' in content)
print('Has retry utility:', 'async def call_bridge_with_retry' in content)
print('Has uuid temp files:', 'uuid.uuid4().hex' in content)

 33 | def _transcribe_sync(file_path: str, language: str):
 34 |     """Synchronous transcription worker executed in a background thread."""
 35 |     whisper_lang = None if language.lower() == "auto" else language
 36 |     segments, info = model.transcribe(
 37 |         file_path,
 38 |         beam_size=5,
 39 |         language=whisper_lang,
 40 |         vad_filter=True,
 41 |     )
 42 |     seg_list = list(segments)
 43 |     text = " ".join(seg.text for seg in seg_list).strip()
 44 |     return info, text, seg_list

 46 | 
 47 | @app.post("/v1/audio/transcriptions")
 48 | async def transcribe(
 49 |     file: UploadFile = File(...),
 50 |     model: str = Form(DEFAULT_MODEL_NAME),   # kept for compatibility with caller
 51 |     language: str = Form("auto"),
 52 |     response_format: str = Form("json"),
 53 | ):
 54 |     """
 55 |     OpenAI-like transcription endpoint (memory-safe & non-blocking).
 56 |     """
 57 |     # Write incoming file to a temporary file in chunks to avoid memory bloat
 58 |     with tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(delete=False, suffix=".wav") as tmp:
 59 |         while True:
 60 |             chunk = await file.read(8192)
 61 |             if not chunk:
 62 |                 break
 63 |             tmp.write(chunk)
 64 |         tmp_path = tmp.name
 65 | 
 66 |     try:
 67 |         # Offload CPU/GPU bound task to prevent blocking the event loop
 68 |         info, text, seg_list = await asyncio.to_thread(_transcribe_sync, tmp_path, language)
 69 |     finally:
 70 |         if os.path.exists(tmp_path):
 71 |             os.remove(tmp_path)
 72 | 
 73 |     if response_format == "json":
 74 |         return JSONResponse(
 75 |             {
 76 |                 "language": info.language,
 77 |                 "text": text,
 78 |                 "segments": [
 79 |                     {
 80 |                         "id": i,
 81 |                         "start": seg.start,
 82 |                         "end": seg.end,
 83 |                         "text": seg.text,
 84 |                     }
 85 |                     for i, seg in enumerate(seg_list)
 86 |                 ],
 87 |             }
 88 |         )
 89 |     else:
 90 |         return text
 91 |

 95 |         app,
 96 |         host="0.0.0.0",

 99 |         reload=False,
100 |     )
